25:T27f2,<entryFree id="n6791" key="جَآءَ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">جَآءَ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">جآء</orth>
                  </form>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَجِىْءُ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">مَجِىْءٌ</foreign> (S, Msb, K, &amp;c., [the most common form, but] deviating from the general rule [respecting inf. ns. of this class], for the inf. n. of a verb of the form <foreign lang="ar">فَعَلَ</foreign> having its aor. of the form <foreign lang="ar">يَفْعِلُ</foreign> is [accord. to the general rule, if commencing with an augmentative <foreign lang="ar">م</foreign>,] <foreign lang="ar">مَفْعَلٌ</foreign>, though some words, beside <foreign lang="ar">مَجِىْءٌ</foreign>, deviate from this rule by being of the measure <foreign lang="ar">مَفْعِلٌ</foreign>, [for <foreign lang="ar">مَجِىْءٌ</foreign> is originally <foreign lang="ar">مَجْيِئٌ</foreign>,] as <foreign lang="ar">مَعِيشٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَكِيلٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَصِيرٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَسِيرٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَحِيدٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَمِيلٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَقِيلٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَزِيدٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَعِيلٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَبِيعٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَحِيصٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَحِيضٌ</foreign>, S, * TA) and <foreign lang="ar">جَيْئَةٌ</foreign> (S, K, of the form of an inf. n. of un., but used as an inf. n. in an absolute sense, like <foreign lang="ar">رَجْفَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">رَحْمَةٌ</foreign>, S, TA) and <foreign lang="ar">جَىْءٌ</foreign>, (K,) <hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, came;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, present;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">أَتَى</foreign>; (S, K;) or <foreign lang="ar">حَضَرَ</foreign>, said of a man [&amp;c.]; (Msb;) or <foreign lang="ar">حَصَلَ</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">it came, came to pass, happened, took place, betided, befell,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">occurred; it resulted; it ensued;</hi> &amp;c.]; and it is used in relation to ideal, as well as real, substantives; so that <foreign lang="ar">إِذَا جَآءَ نَصْرُ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">When the assistance of God shall come</hi> (in the Kur ex. 1)] is [not a figurative but] a proper phrase. (Er-Rághib, TA.) Sb mentions, on the authority of certain of the Arabs, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ يَجِيكَ</foreign> [for <foreign lang="ar">هو يَجِيْؤُكَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He comes,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">will come, to thee</hi>], with the hemzeh suppressed: (TA:) and he also mentions <foreign lang="ar">يَجُوْءُ</foreign> as a dial. var. of <foreign lang="ar">يَجِىْءُ</foreign>. (Id. in art. <foreign lang="ar">جوأ</foreign>, q. v.) [As shown above,] <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ</foreign> is used intransitively and transitively. (Msb, MF.) say, <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ زَيْدٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Zeyd came;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, present.</hi> (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">جِئْتُ مَجِيْئًا حَسَنًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I came with a good coming;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in a good manner</hi>]. (S.) And <foreign lang="ar">جِئْتُ زَيْدًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I came to Zeyd.</hi> (Msb.) And sometimes one says, <foreign lang="ar">جِئْتُ إِلَيْهِ</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">I went</hi> [as well as <hi rend="ital">I came</hi>] <hi rend="ital">to him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it.</hi> (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">جِئْتُ مِنَ البَلَدِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I came from the town,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">country</hi>]: and <foreign lang="ar">مِنَ القَوْمِ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ عِنْدِ القَوْمِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">from the presence of the people,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">company of men</hi>]. (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الغَيْثُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The rain</hi> [<hi rend="ital">came,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">descended.</hi> (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ أَمْرُ السُّلْطَانِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The order,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">command, of the Sultán came,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">arrived.</hi> (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">جِئْتُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِهِ</foreign> (S, Msb, K) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n6791-1" target="أَجَأْتُهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, both signifying the same, (S, K,) [<hi rend="ital">I came with him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">I brought him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, with me.</hi> (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">الحَمْدُ للّٰهِ الَّذِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ بِكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Praise be to God who brought thee</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar">الحَمْدُ للّٰهِ إِذْ جِئْتَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Praise be to God because,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">that, thou camest,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hast come</hi>]; but not <foreign lang="ar">الحَمْدُ للّٰهِ الَّذِى جِئْتَ</foreign>: (S, TA:) and [in like manner] you say, <foreign lang="ar">الحَمْدُ للّٰهِ إِذْ كَانَ كَذَا</foreign>; but not <foreign lang="ar">الحَمْدُ للّٰهِ الَّذِى كَانَ كَذَا</foreign> unless you say <foreign lang="ar">بِهِ</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">مِنْهُ</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">عَنْهُ</foreign> [after <foreign lang="ar">الذى</foreign>]. (ISk, TA.) [Hence, <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ بِوَلَدٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He begot a child,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">children;</hi> like <foreign lang="ar">أَتَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِوَلَدٍ</foreign>. And <foreign lang="ar">جَآءتْ بِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">She brought him forth; gave birth to him;</hi> like <foreign lang="ar">أَتَتْ بِهِ</foreign>. And <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ بِمَعْنًى</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a word) <hi rend="ital">conveyed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">imported, a meaning.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [<foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ بِشَىْءٍ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">He brought to pass, did, executed, performed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">effected, a thing:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">he said, gave utterance to,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">uttered, a thing:</hi> like <foreign lang="ar">أَتَى بِهِ</foreign> in both these senses.] And <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ كَذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He did thus,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">such a thing.</hi> (TA.) Hence, [in the Kur xix. 28,] <foreign lang="ar">لَقَدْ جِئْتِ شَيْئًا فَرِيًّا</foreign> (TA) [<hi rend="ital">Verily,</hi> O Mary, <hi rend="ital">thou hast done</hi>] <hi rend="ital">a thing hitherto unknown; a thing deemed strange.</hi> (Bd. [See another ex. voce <foreign lang="ar">إِمْرٌ</foreign>, likewise from the Kur.]) And <foreign lang="ar">جِئْتُ شَيْئًا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حَسَنًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I did a good thing.</hi> (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ بِالبَدِيعِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He produced a new saying,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">new poetry, not after the similitude of anything preceding.</hi> (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">بدع</foreign>.) And <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ جَرْيًا بَعْدَ جَرْىٍ</foreign> (K in art. <foreign lang="ar">تأم</foreign>) or [more commonly] <foreign lang="ar">جاء بِجَرْىٍ بَعْدَ جَرْىٍ</foreign> (M in that art.) [<hi rend="ital">He</hi> (a horse) <hi rend="ital">performed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">fetched, run after run</hi>].          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">جَآء</foreign> is also <hi rend="ital">syn. with</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">صَارَ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">أَتَى</foreign>; as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ البِنَآءُ مُحْكَمًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The building became,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">came to be, firm, strong,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">compact.</hi> (Kull p. 11.) [And hence the phrase,] <foreign lang="ar">مَا جَآءَتْ حَاجَتَكَ</foreign>, (M, K,) thus in all the copies of the K, with the noun in the accus. case; i. e. <hi rend="ital">What became,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">has become, thy want?</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">مَا صَارَتْ</foreign>; (M, K;) or <hi rend="ital">What was thy want?</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">مَا كَانَتْ</foreign>: (Er-Radee, TA:) <foreign lang="ar">ما</foreign> being here an interrogative, and the [implied] pronoun [in the verb] being made fem. because its predicate is fem.: but some say <foreign lang="ar">حَاجَتُكَ</foreign>, in the nom. case, [as it is in the CK, meaning <hi rend="ital">What did,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">has, thy want become?</hi>] regarding <foreign lang="ar">حاجتك</foreign> as the subject of <foreign lang="ar">جاءت</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">ما</foreign> as the predicate of this verb. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  See also 3.    </entryFree>26:Tb62,<entryFree id="n6792" key="مُجَايَأَةٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>3</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">مُجَايَأَةٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> [inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">جَايَأَ</foreign>] signifies The act of <hi rend="ital">facing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">fronting; being opposite,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">over against:</hi> (IAar, K:) and the act of <hi rend="ital">coinciding;</hi> as also <foreign lang="ar">جِيَآءٌ</foreign>. (AZ, K.) You say of a man, <foreign lang="ar">جَايَأَنِى مِنْ قُرْبٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He faced me, fronted me, was opposite to me,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">was over against me, at a short distance.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّ بِى مُجَايَأَةً</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He passed by me being in front,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">opposite.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">جَايَأْتُ فُلَانًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I coincided with such a one in his coming.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">لَوْ جَاوَزْتَ هٰذَا المَكَانَ لَجَايَأْتَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الغَيْثَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Hadst thou passed beyond this place, thou hadst met with rain,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">coincided with rain in its coming.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>    
      <foreign lang="ar">جَاآنِى <ref cref="n6792-1" target="فَجِئْتُهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="SO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, [so in copies of the S, and in copies of the K, as from the S, but in the TA, as from the S, <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَأَنِى</foreign>, and said to be with two hemzehs, though this is evidently wrong,] aor. <foreign lang="ar">أَجِيْؤُهُ</foreign>, the former verb of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَاعَلَنِى</foreign>, (S,) is [said to be] a mistake for <foreign lang="ar">جَايَأَنِى فجئته</foreign>, since the former verb has an infirm letter [<foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>] for its medial radical and <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign> for its final, not the reverse, (Sgh, K,) [therefore] what J says is not allowable unless it be an instance of transposition; (IB, TA;) but what is given by F [and Sgh as the correct form] is that which is accord. to rule, and what J says is that which has been heard from the Arabs, as ISd has pointed out; (TA;) [and rule is not to be regarded when it is contr. to classical usage;] the meaning is, <hi rend="ital">He vied with me,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">strove to surpass me, in frequency of coming, and I surpassed him therein.</hi> (S, K.)    </entryFree>27:T763,<entryFree id="n6793" key="أَجَاءَهُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>4</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">أَجَاءَهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He made him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, to come.</hi> (Kull p. 11.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">أَجَأْتُهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">جِئْتُ بِهِ</foreign>: see 1. (S, K.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">أَجَأْتُهُ إِلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I compelled him, constrained him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">necessitated him, to have recourse,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">betake himself, to it;</hi> (Fr, S, K;) or <hi rend="ital">made him to want it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">be in need of it:</hi> (S:) in the dial. of Temeem, <foreign lang="ar">أَشَأْتُهُ</foreign>. (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">شيأ</foreign>.) It is said in a prov., <foreign lang="ar">شَرٌّ مَا يُجِيْؤُكَ إِلَى مُخَّةِ عُرْقُوبٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">It is an evil thing that compels thee to have recourse to the marrow of a hock</hi>]; for, as As says, the <foreign lang="ar">عرقوب</foreign> contains no marrow, and only he who cannot obtain any [other] thing is made to want it. (S.) And it is said in the Kur xix. 23, <foreign lang="ar">فَأَجَآءَهَا المَخَاضُ إِلَى جِذْعِ النَّخْلَةِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">And the motion of the child in her womb compelled her to betake herself to the trunk of the palm-tree.</hi> (Bd.)    </entryFree>28:T508,<entryFree id="n6796" key="جَيَّآءٌ" type="main">
